[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mTo solve this problem, we need to express the number of moles of gas \(n\) in terms of the metal volume \(V_m\), temperature \(T\), gas constant \(R\), and tensile strength \(\sigma\).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 1: Relate wall thickness to metal volume.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThe volume of the metal \(V_m\) used to construct a spherical pressure vessel with radius \(r\) and wall thickness \(t\) (assuming thin walls, so \(t \ll r\)) is given by the surface area of the sphere multiplied by the thickness:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ V_m = 4\pi r^2 t \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mFrom this, we can express the thickness \(t\) in terms of \(V_m\) and \(r\):[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ t = \frac{V_m}{4\pi r^2} \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 2: Relate pressure to tensile strength.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mFor a thin-walled spherical pressure vessel, the relationship between the internal pressure \(P\), the radius \(r\), wall thickness \(t\), and the tensile strength (hoop stress) \(\sigma\) is given by:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ \sigma = \frac{Pr}{2t} \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSolving for pressure \(P\):[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ P = \frac{2\sigma t}{r} \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubstitute the expression for \(t\) from Step 1 into this equation:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ P = \frac{2\sigma}{r} \left( \frac{V_m}{4\pi r^2} \right) = \frac{2 V_m \sigma}{4\pi r^3} = \frac{V_m \sigma}{2\pi r^3} \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 3: Relate internal volume to radius.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThe internal volume of the spherical vessel \(V_{\text{vessel}}\) is:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ V_{\text{vessel}} = \frac{4}{3}\pi r^3 \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 4: Apply the Ideal Gas Law.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThe ideal gas law is given by \(PV = nRT\). Here, \(P\) is the pressure, \(V\) is the internal volume \(V_{\text{vessel}}\), \(n\) is the number of moles, \(R\) is the ideal gas constant, and \(T\) is the temperature.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubstituting the expressions for \(P\) and \(V_{\text{vessel}}\):[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ \left( \frac{V_m \sigma}{2\pi r^3} \right) \left( \frac{4}{3}\pi r^3 \right) = nRT \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 5: Simplify and solve for \(n\).**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mCancel the common terms (\(\pi r^3\)) from the numerator and denominator:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ \frac{V_m \sigma}{2} \cdot \frac{4}{3} = nRT \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ \frac{4 V_m \sigma}{6} = nRT \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ \frac{2 V_m \sigma}{3} = nRT \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mIsolate \(n\):[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ n = \frac{2 V_m \sigma}{3 RT} \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mRewrite this in the form \(\frac{k}{m} \times \frac{V_m\sigma}{RT}\):[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\[ n = \frac{2}{3} \times \frac{V_m\sigma}{RT} \][0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m(Note: The prompt mentions the form \(\frac{k}{m} \times \frac{V_m\sigma}{RTn}\). Since \(n\) is the variable we are solving for, the \(n\) in the denominator of the prompt's form is likely a typo for 1 or a placeholder for the variable's exponent. Given the derived formula does not contain \(n\) in the denominator, we treat the coefficient part as the relevant structure).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mComparing \(n = \frac{2}{3} \frac{V_m\sigma}{RT}\) to the form \(\frac{k}{m} \frac{V_m\sigma}{RT}\), we identify:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\(k = 2\)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m\(m = 3\)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThe problem asks for the value of \(k + m + n\). In the context of such algebraic forms where the variable \(n\) is the subject, \(n\) in the sum typically refers to the exponent of \(n\) in the expression or simply the integer 1 (representing the variable \(n\) itself on the LHS). However, often in these problems, if the form is \(\frac{k}{m} \frac{V_m\sigma}{RT}\), the "n" in the sum \(k+m+n\) refers to the variable name's exponent if explicitly written, or it implies the sum of the coefficients and the variable count/parameter count.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mGiven the typo in the prompt "RTn" likely meant "RT", and the variable is \(n\), the most consistent interpretation for the third term is 1 (the power of \(n\) on the LHS, or the number of moles parameter).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThus, \(k=2\), \(m=3\), and \(n=1\).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSum \(= 2 + 3 + 1 = 6\).[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's break it down by the forced moves.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges incident to $C$ are $CB$ and $CD$. Since the degree of $C$ is 2, the path must use both. So the sub-path $B-C-D$ or $D-C-B$ is mandatory.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges incident to $E$ are $EA$ and $ED$. Since the degree of $E$ is 2, the path must use both. So the sub-path $A-E-D$ or $D-E-A$ is mandatory.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m1.  $B \leftrightarrow C \leftrightarrow D$ (order depends on direction)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m2.  $A \leftrightarrow E \leftrightarrow D$ (order depends on direction)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNow let's reconstruct the path.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe path starts at $A$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe vertices $C$ and $E$ are "bridges" between $B, D$ and $A, D$ respectively.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mActually, since it's an Eulerian path, we must use *all* edges exactly once.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's look at the degrees again.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's break the graph into cycles or chains.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe are at $A$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's try to build the path.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges incident to $E$: $e_1 = AE, e_2 = DE$. Path must contain sequence $A-E-D$ or $D-E-A$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's look at the "forced" moves at $C$ and $E$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mRemoving $C$ merges $B$ and $D$ with a constraint that we traverse $BC$ then $CD$ (or vice versa). This effectively adds a "virtual" edge between $B$ and $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mRemoving $E$ merges $A$ and $D$ with a constraint that we traverse $AE$ then $ED$ (or vice versa). This effectively adds a "virtual" edge between $A$ and $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's construct a multigraph (or simply consider the sequence of vertices) based on this.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe path visits:[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's analyze the constraints on $D$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSpecifically:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$D-C-B$ is a path of length 2.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$D-E-A$ is a path of length 2.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges directly connecting $D$: $DA, DB$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's think of the graph as having vertices $A, B, D$ with "thick" edges connecting them due to $C$ and $E$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- Edge between $B$ and $D$ via $C$: Path $B-C-D$ (2 edges).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- Edge between $D$ and $A$ via $E$: Path $D-E-A$ (2 edges).[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mHowever, since $C$ and $E$ must be visited, they act as bridges between specific pairs.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$C$ bridges $B$ and $D$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince we must visit $E$, and $E$ only connects to $A$ and $D$, we must traverse the path $A-E-D$ or $D-E-A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf the path contains $A-E-D$, we arrive at $D$ from $E$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf the path contains $D-E-A$, we arrive at $A$ from $E$ (and leave to $D$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's consider the three segments connecting the "main" vertices $A, B, D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m1. Segment $S_1$: $B-C-D$ (or $D-C-B$). This is a sequence of 2 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m2. Segment $S_2$: $A-E-D$ (or $D-E-A$). This is a sequence of 2 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m3. Direct edges: $e_3=AB, e_4=AD, e_5=BD$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$S_1$ uses 2 edges ($BC, CD$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$S_2$ uses 2 edges ($AE, DE$).[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mTotal $2+2+3 = 7$. Correct.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe path must visit $A$ and end at $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe graph can be viewed as a multigraph with vertices $A, B, D$ and edges:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- Two edges between $B$ and $D$ (representing path via $C$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- Two edges between $A$ and $D$ (representing path via $E$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- One edge between $A$ and $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- One edge between $A$ and $D$ (direct).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- One edge between $B$ and $D$ (direct).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's count degrees in this "reduced" graph (vertices $A, B, D$):[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- Connected to $B$ (1 edge)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- Connected to $D$ (1 direct edge)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- Connected to $D$ (via $E$). The edges are $AE$ and $ED$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, in the reduced graph logic, we are looking for a trail that visits each "super-edge" or "path segment".[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut the original graph is just a graph. Let's just trace the path.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's denote the path as a sequence of vertices.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mStart at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mMust visit $E$ (since it has degree 2). The path must contain the subsequence $A-E-D$ or $D-E-A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince we start at $A$, if we visit $E$ first, we go $A \to E \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we don't visit $E$ first, we must visit $E$ later. But to visit $E$, we must come from $A$ or $D$ and leave to $D$ or $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mCase 1: First segment is $A \to E \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mCase 2: We visit $E$ later. Since we start at $A$, and $E$ connects $A$ and $D$, to reach $E$ without traversing $AE$ yet, we must have reached $A$ or $D$ somehow.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut we start at $A$. So we leave $A$ via some edge.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges from $A$: $AB, AD, AE$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSubcase 2a: Leave $A$ via $AB$. Then we are at $B$. From $B$, we can go to $C$ or $D$ (using $BD$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSubcase 2b: Leave $A$ via $AD$. Then we are at $D$. From $D$, we can go to $C$, $E$, or $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSubcase 2c: Leave $A$ via $AE$. This is Case 1.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's analyze Case 1: Start with $A \to E \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mPath so far: $A, E, D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges used: $AE, ED$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mCurrent vertex: $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mRemaining edges to use: $AB, AD, BC, BD, CD$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $AD$ is still available.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe are at $D$. We need to end at $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAnd we must use $BC, CD$ (the path via $C$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAnd $AD$ (direct to A).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAnd $BD$ (direct to B).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAnd $AB$ (direct to B).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe have used $AE, ED$. We need to use $BC, CD$. This is a path $B-C-D$ or $D-C-B$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mVertices $A, B, D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- 1 between $A, B$ ($AB$)[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- 1 between $B, D$ ($BD$)[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$: $1 (AB) + 1 (AD) + 1 (AE-D) = 3$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B$: $1 (AB) + 1 (BD) + 1 (B-C-D) = 3$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$D$: $1 (AD) + 1 (AE-D) + 1 (BD) + 1 (B-C-D) = 4$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mDegrees match the odd/even constraint.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mStart $A$, End $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we are looking for the number of Eulerian paths in this multigraph from $A$ to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's label the edges in the multigraph to keep track of which original edges they correspond to.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet edges be:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $x = AB$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $y = AD$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $z = AD'$ (path $A-E-D$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $w = BD$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $v = BD'$ (path $B-C-D$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need a trail $A \to \dots \to B$ using $x, y, z, w, v$ exactly once.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we use $z$, we are traversing $A-E-D$. This consumes $AE$ and $ED$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we use $v$, we are traversing $B-C-D$. This consumes $BC$ and $CD$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we use $y$, we consume $AD$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we use $w$, we consume $BD$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we use $x$, we consume $AB$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, there is a subtle issue.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWhen we traverse the edge $z$ (macro $A-E-D$) in the multigraph, we are effectively saying "traverse $AE$ then $ED$".[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis implies we are at $A$, go to $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut in the original graph, $E$ is a vertex.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIs it possible to visit $E$ differently? No, degree 2.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo yes, traversing the macro edge corresponds to traversing the specific 2 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mHowever, does the order matter?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we traverse $z$, it contributes $AE, ED$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we traverse $z$ in reverse (as $D-E-A$), it contributes $DE, EA$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIn an undirected multigraph, we just traverse the edge. The internal structure (E) is fixed.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, for $z$ ($A-E-D$), the path is $A \to E \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mFor $v$ ($B-C-D$), the path is $B \to C \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut we can traverse them in reverse?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we have edge $z$ between $A$ and $D$, can we traverse it as $D \to A$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIn the original graph, $D-E-A$ is the reverse of $A-E-D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mYes, we can traverse it as $D \to E \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo $z$ represents the connection between $A$ and $D$ via $E$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSimilarly $v$ represents the connection between $B$ and $D$ via $C$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the problem reduces to:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mFind the number of Eulerian paths in the multigraph $M$ with vertices $\{A, B, D\}$ and edges $\{AB, AD, AD_E, BD, BD_C\}$ from $A$ to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, is it that simple?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's check.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSuppose we have a path in $M$: $A \to B \to D \to A \to D \to B$ (using edges $x, w, z, y, v$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges used:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$x$ ($AB$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$w$ ($BD$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$z$ ($A-E-D$) ? Wait, edge $z$ connects $A$ and $D$. If we traverse $D \to A$ in $M$ using $z$, it corresponds to $D \to E \to A$ in original.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$y$ ($AD$) ? Edge $y$ connects $A$ and $D$. Traversing $A \to D$ in $M$ corresponds to $A \to D$ in original.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$v$ ($BD$) ? Edge $v$ connects $B$ and $D$. Traversing $D \to B$ in $M$ corresponds to $D \to C \to B$ in original.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's check the sequence in $M$: $A \xrightarrow{x} B \xrightarrow{w} D \xrightarrow{z} A \xrightarrow{y} D \xrightarrow{v} B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m1. $AB$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m2. $BD$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m3. $D \to E \to A$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m4. $A \to D$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m5. $D \to C \to B$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mTotal edges: $AB, BD, DE, EA, AD, DC, CB$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mOriginal edges: $AB, AD, AE, BC, BD, CD, DE$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mMy list: $AB, BD, DE, EA, AD, DC, CB$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mMatches.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIs it a valid path?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mYes.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the mapping seems valid.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, is there any constraint on the order of $z$ and $v$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNo, they are just edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mHowever, $z$ involves $E$ and $v$ involves $C$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIs it possible that traversing $z$ (as $A-E-D$) interferes with traversing $v$ (as $B-C-D$)?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIn the multigraph, vertices are $A, B, D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we traverse $z$ as $A \to D$, we are at $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we traverse $v$ as $D \to B$, we leave $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis seems consistent.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, what if we traverse $z$ as $D \to A$? We enter $D$ and leave to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWhat if we traverse $v$ as $B \to D$? We enter $B$ and leave to $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis seems consistent.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, is there any case where the macro-graph abstraction fails?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe only assumption is that we cannot visit $E$ or $C$ in a way that splits the macro edge.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince $E$ and $C$ have degree 2, any path entering them must use both incident edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThus, they always form a "bridge" between their neighbors.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the reduction to the multigraph on $\{A, B, D\}$ seems perfectly valid.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges of the multigraph are:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $e_1 = AB$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $e_2 = AD$ (direct)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $e_3 = AD_E$ (via $E$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $e_4 = BD$ (direct)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m- $e_5 = BD_C$ (via $C$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mTotal 5 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mStart node $A$, end node $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mDegrees in multigraph:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$: connected to $B$ (1), $D$ (2). Total 3.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B$: connected to $A$ (1), $D$ (2). Total 3.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$D$: connected to $A$ (2), $B$ (2). Total 4.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mOdd degree nodes: $A, B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEulerian path exists.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we need to count the number of Eulerian paths from $A$ to $B$ in this multigraph.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's analyze the structure.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIt's a graph with 3 vertices.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$ is connected to $D$ twice (edges 2 and 3).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B$ is connected to $D$ twice (edges 4 and 5).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$ is connected to $B$ once (edge 1).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's denote the edges between $A$ and $D$ as $d_A$ and $d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's denote the edges between $B$ and $D$ as $d_B$ and $d'_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet the edge between $A$ and $B$ be $a$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe want a path $A \to \dots \to B$ using $\{a, d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$ once.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's break it down by the usage of edge $a$ ($AB$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIn any Eulerian path, we must traverse $a$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince $a$ connects $A$ and $B$, it can be traversed as $A \to B$ or $B \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m**Case 1: $A \to B$ is the last edge.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the path ends with $A \to B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need a path from $A$ to $A$ using the remaining edges $\{d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, if we end with $A \to B$, the start is $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we need a cycle from $A$ to $A$ using the edges connecting $A$ and $D$ and $B$ and $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, the edges incident to $B$ in the remaining set are $d_B, d'_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must go $A \to \dots \to B \to A$? No.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf the path ends at $B$ via $A \to B$, then just before this we were at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we need an Eulerian path from $A$ to $A$ using $\{d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNo, that would imply we start at $A$ and end at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut the edges $\{d_B, d'_B\}$ are incident to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we use $A \to B$ at the very end, then $B$ is visited at the end.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBefore that, we must have been at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the prefix is a path from $A$ to $A$ using $\{d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, in the prefix, we must start at $A$ (since we are at $A$ before taking $A \to B$) and end at $A$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNo. The full path is $A \to \dots \to A \to B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the prefix must be a cycle starting and ending at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mDoes the set $\{d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$ form a cycle on $A$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges connect $A$ and $B$ to $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the subgraph on $A, B, D$ has these edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$ connects to $D$ (twice).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B$ connects to $D$ (twice).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mTo form a cycle from $A$ to $A$, we must go $A \to D \dots \to D \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must use the edges incident to $A$. These are $d_A, d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must leave $A$ via one, and return via the other.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the cycle must look like $A \xrightarrow{d_A} D \dots \xrightarrow{d'_A} A$? No, the direction matters.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mOr $A \xrightarrow{d_A} D \to \dots \to D \xrightarrow{d'_A} A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $d_A$ connects $A$ and $D$. $d'_A$ connects $A$ and $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mTo form a cycle starting at $A$, we use edges incident to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges incident to $A$ in the set $\{d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$ are $d_A, d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $d_B, d'_B$ are incident to $B$ and $D$. They are not incident to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo, to form a cycle using ALL edges, we must enter and leave $A$ and $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut $B$ is not the starting point of the cycle (it's the end of the whole path).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait. If we use edge $a$ ($AB$) as the last step, then the prefix is a trail using $\{d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$ from $A$ to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis means the trail starts at $A$, visits all edges, and returns to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges available are $d_A, d'_A$ (incident to $A, D$) and $d_B, d'_B$ (incident to $B, D$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $B$ has degree 2 in this subgraph (edges $d_B, d'_B$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo to traverse all edges incident to $B$ ($d_B, d'_B$), the path must enter $B$ and leave $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut we start at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the path must go $A \to \dots \to B \to \dots \to B \to \dots \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, can we visit $B$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mYes.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the path is $A \to D \to \dots \to B \to \dots \to D \to \dots \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mActually, the structure is a set of cycles.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's visualize the multigraph again.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$ is connected to $D$ with 2 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B$ is connected to $D$ with 2 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$ and $B$ are not connected in the prefix subgraph (since $a$ is removed).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the prefix subgraph is just $A-D$ (2 edges) and $B-D$ (2 edges).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo it's a "theta" graph or just two parallel edges between $A,D$ and two parallel edges between $B,D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mVertices $A, B, D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need an Eulerian path from $A$ to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mDegrees in this subgraph:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A$: 2 (connected to $D$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B$: 2 (connected to $D$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$D$: 4 (connected to $A$ twice, $B$ twice)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAll degrees are even. So Eulerian circuits exist.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince the graph is connected (it's connected at $D$), we can form a circuit.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe graph consists of two loops sharing a vertex? No.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIt looks like a "ladder" or "H" shape rotated?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A-D$ (1)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A-D$ (2)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B-D$ (1)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$B-D$ (2)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need to traverse all 5 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, 4 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need to traverse $d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mStart at $A$, end at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince $A$ has degree 2, we must enter and leave $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must pick one edge from $\{d_A, d'_A\}$ to leave $A$, and one to return to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, since $d_A, d'_A$ are the only edges incident to $A$, we must traverse both.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mOne goes $A \to D$, the other $D \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we have a "loop" $A \to D \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, the edges are distinct.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we traverse one $A \to D$, say $d_A$, then at $D$ we must continue to $B$ (since we can't end at $D$, and we need to use $d_B, d'_B$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $B$ must also be visited. $B$ has degree 2 ($d_B, d'_B$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must enter $B$ and leave $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo from $D$, we can go to $B$ via $d_B$ or $d'_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSuppose we go $D \to B$ via $d_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $B$, we must leave via $d'_B$ to $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $D$, we have remaining edges $d'_A$ (incident to $A$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we go $D \to A$ via $d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis completes the cycle.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's check the sequence of edges:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m1. $A \to D$ (using $d_A$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m2. $D \to B$ (using $d_B$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m3. $B \to D$ (using $d'_B$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m4. $D \to A$ (using $d'_A$)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis uses all 4 edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mStart $A$, end $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis is a valid prefix.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAre there other orderings?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $D$, we have arrived from $A$ via $d_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAvailable edges at $D$: $d'_A, d_B, d'_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need to visit $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe can go to $B$ via $d_B$ or $d'_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we go $D \to B$ via $d_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $B$, we have only $d'_B$ left. So $B \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $D$, we have $d'_A$ left. So $D \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis forms the cycle: $A \to D \to B \to D \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges are $d_A, d_B, d'_B, d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis uses all edges.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mCould we do $A \to D \to A$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNo, we must use $d_B, d'_B$ as well.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we go $A \to D \to A$, we used $d_A, d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe are back at $A$. But we still have $d_B, d'_B$ unused.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince $B$ is isolated from $A$ in this subgraph, we can't reach $B$ from $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo this is not a valid Eulerian path (it would get stuck at $A$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the path must go to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the cycle must be $A \to D \to B \to D \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIs it possible to traverse $A \to D \to A$ then jump to $B$? No, connected component.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, is it possible to traverse $d_A$ then $d_B$ then $d'_A$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$A \xrightarrow{d_A} D \xrightarrow{d_B} B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $B$, we must leave via $d'_B$. So $B \xrightarrow{d'_B} D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $D$, we have $d'_A$. So $D \xrightarrow{d'_A} A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis is the only "topology" of the traversal because $A$ is a "leaf" in the sense that we must enter/leave via the two edges. Same for $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the sequence of edges is constrained to be:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEnter $A$ via $d_A$ (wait, we start at $A$, so leave $A$ via $d_A$ or $d'_A$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's say we leave via $d_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThen at $D$, we must go to $B$ (since if we go to $A$ we close the loop and miss $B$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must go to $B$. We have 2 edges to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's say we go $D \to B$ via $d_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThen at $B$, we must leave via $d'_B$. So $B \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $D$, we must go to $A$ via $d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the path is $A \xrightarrow{d_A} D \xrightarrow{d_B} B \xrightarrow{d'_B} D \xrightarrow{d'_A} A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIs it possible to swap $d_A$ and $d'_A$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mYes, we could start with $d'_A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThen $A \xrightarrow{d'_A} D \xrightarrow{d_B} B \xrightarrow{d'_B} D \xrightarrow{d_A} A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIs it possible to swap $d_B$ and $d'_B$?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mYes, $D \xrightarrow{d'_B} B \xrightarrow{d_B} D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo there are $2 \times 2 = 4$ such paths.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's verify.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe set of edges is $\{d_A, d'_A, d_B, d'_B\}$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe path must be a cycle.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince $A$ has only neighbors $D$ in this subgraph, we must use $d_A, d'_A$ to connect to $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the path enters $A$ and leaves $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSimilarly for $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the sequence must be $A \leftrightarrow D \leftrightarrow B \leftrightarrow D \leftrightarrow A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $D$ has degree 4. We enter $D$ from $A$, leave to $B$. Then enter from $B$, leave to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the structure is fixed: $A-D-B-D-A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe can order the edges incident to $A$: 2 choices ($d_A$ first, $d'_A$ first).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe can order the edges incident to $B$: 2 choices ($d_B$ first, $d'_B$ first).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe edges incident to $D$ are fixed by the choices at $A$ and $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, let's trace carefully.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mPath: $A \xrightarrow{e_1} D \xrightarrow{e_2} B \xrightarrow{e_3} D \xrightarrow{e_4} A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$e_1 \in \{d_A, d'_A\}$. (2 choices)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$e_4 \in \{d_A, d'_A\} \setminus \{e_1\}$. (1 choice)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $D$ (after $e_1$), we must go to $B$ (since if we go to $A$ we stop).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges incident to $B$ are $d_B, d'_B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe arrive at $B$ via $e_2 \in \{d_B, d'_B\}$. (2 choices)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThen we leave $B$ via $e_3 \in \{d_B, d'_B\} \setminus \{e_2\}$. (1 choice)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAt $D$ (after $e_3$), we must go to $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mRemaining edge is $e_4$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo, total number of paths from $A$ to $A$ is $2 \times 2 = 4$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThese correspond to the prefix paths.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThen we append the final edge $A \to B$ (which is edge $x$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we have **4 solutions** ending in $A \to B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m**Case 2: $B \to A$ is used?**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNo, we start at $A$ and end at $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the edge $AB$ (edge $x$) must be traversed either as $A \to B$ or $B \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we traverse $x$ as $B \to A$, then we arrive at $A$ from $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut we start at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis implies we must leave $A$ via some other edges, and eventually return to $A$ from $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, if we traverse $B \to A$, then the edge $x$ is used as the *last* step of the "A-side" of the path?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, the path starts at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we leave $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe eventually traverse $x$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we traverse $x$ as $B \to A$, then we are at $A$ after traversing $x$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut we need to end at $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo $x$ cannot be the last edge of the path if it is traversed as $B \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, if we traverse $x$ as $B \to A$, we are at $A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThen we must continue to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut the only edge connecting $A$ to $B$ is $x$ (and maybe others? No, only $x$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo if we are at $A$ and need to go to $B$, we must take $x$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut we already took $x$ (as $B \to A$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSince edges must be used exactly once, we cannot take $x$ again.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mTherefore, we cannot be at $A$ after taking $x$ as $B \to A$ and then need to go to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, unless there is another path from $A$ to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIn the multigraph, is there another path?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNo, $A$ is only connected to $D$ in the remaining graph (excluding $x$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $A$ connects to $D$ (2 edges). $B$ connects to $D$ (2 edges).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThere is no direct edge $A \to B$ other than $x$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo, if we take $x$ as $B \to A$, we are at $A$. The only way to get to $B$ is via $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must go $A \to D \to B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIs there a path from $A$ to $B$ using the remaining edges?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mYes. The remaining edges are $d_A, d'_A$ (connect $A, D$) and $d_B, d'_B$ (connect $B, D$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe can go $A \to D$ (using $d_A$) then $D \to B$ (using $d_B$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo, $A \xrightarrow{d_A} D \xrightarrow{d_B} B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis gets us to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the edge $x$ ($A \to B$) must be traversed either at the very end or somewhere in the middle.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, I assumed earlier that $x$ must be traversed.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we traverse $x$ as $A \to B$, it's at the end? Not necessarily.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut in Case 1, I assumed $A \to B$ is the *last* edge.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf $A \to B$ is not the last edge, say we use $A \to B$ then go somewhere else?[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mFrom $B$, we can go to $D$ (using $d_B$ or $d'_B$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we can go $A \to B \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mBut wait, in my previous analysis, I considered the multigraph.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe vertices are $A, B, D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges: $x (AB)$, $y, y' (AD)$, $z, z' (BD)$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mIf we start at $A$, we can take $x$ ($A \to B$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThen from $B$ we must take $z$ or $z'$ (to go to $D$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSuppose $A \to B \to D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe are at $D$. Remaining edges: $y, y'$ (at $A, D$) and $z', z''$ (at $B, D$). Wait, $z$ and $z'$ are the two edges $BD$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's call edges between $B, D$ as $u_1, u_2$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges between $A, D$ as $v_1, v_2$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mEdges between $A, B$ is $w$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mStart $A$. End $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mPath must use $w, v_1, v_2, u_1, u_2$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's enumerate based on the position of $w$ (edge $AB$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m$w$ can be traversed as $A \to B$ or $B \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33m**Subcase 2.1: $w$ is traversed as $A \to B$.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe path starts $A \to B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mNow we are at $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mRemaining edges: $v_1, v_2$ (between $A, D$) and $u_1, u_2$ (between $B, D$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need to end at $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must form a path from $B$ to $B$ using $v_1, v_2, u_1, u_2$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThe graph of remaining edges connects $A$ and $D$ via $v$'s, and $B$ and $D$ via $u$'s.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait, $v$'s connect $A$ and $D$. $u$'s connect $B$ and $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the path must go $B \to D \to A \to D \to B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's check connectivity.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mStart $B$. Must take a $u$ edge to $D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSay $B \xrightarrow{u_1} D$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mFrom $D$, we must go to $A$ (since we need to use $v$'s which are incident to $A$).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mFrom $D$, take $v_1$ to $A$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mFrom $D$, take $u_2$ to $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mThis closes the loop at $B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo the sequence is $A \xrightarrow{w} B \xrightarrow{u_1} D \xrightarrow{v_1} A \xrightarrow{v_2} D \xrightarrow{u_2} B$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mLet's check if this is valid.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mAll distinct?[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWait.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mWe need to eventually traverse $w$ as $B \to A$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [33mSo we must reach $B$.[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mTo solve the problem, we need to find the number of points $(x, y)$ on the graph of the equation $y=(x+2)^4-100$ such that both $x$ and $y$ are negative integers.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 1: Analyze the conditions for $x$ and $y$.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThe problem states that both coordinates must be negative integers.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m1.  $x$ must be an integer and $x < 0$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m2.  $y$ must be an integer and $y < 0$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 2: Use the equation to find the condition for $y < 0$.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubstitute the equation for $y$ into the inequality $y < 0$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$(x+2)^4 - 100 < 0$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$(x+2)^4 < 100$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 3: Determine the integer values for $x$ that satisfy the inequality.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSince $x$ is an integer, $(x+2)$ is an integer. Let $u = x+2$. We are looking for integer values of $u$ such that $u^4 < 100$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mLet's test integer values for $|u|$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $|u| = 1$, $u^4 = 1 < 100$ (Valid)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $|u| = 2$, $u^4 = 16 < 100$ (Valid)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $|u| = 3$, $u^4 = 81 < 100$ (Valid)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $|u| = 4$, $u^4 = 256 > 100$ (Invalid)[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThus, the possible integer values for $u$ are $\{-3, -2, -1, 0, 1, 2, 3\}$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 4: Convert back to $x$ values.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSince $u = x+2$, we have $x = u - 2$. We calculate $x$ for each valid $u$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $u = -3$, $x = -5$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $u = -2$, $x = -4$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $u = -1$, $x = -3$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $u = 0$, $x = -2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $u = 1$, $x = -1$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $u = 2$, $x = 0$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   If $u = 3$, $x = 1$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 5: Apply the condition that $x$ must be a negative integer.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mFrom the list of possible $x$ values $\{-5, -4, -3, -2, -1, 0, 1\}$, we must select those strictly less than 0.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThe negative integers are:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   $x = -5$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   $x = -4$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   $x = -3$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   $x = -2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   $x = -1$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 6: Verify the corresponding $y$ values.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mFor each valid $x$, we check if $y$ is a negative integer. Since $y = (x+2)^4 - 100$ and $(x+2)^4 < 100$, $y$ will always be negative. Since $x$ is an integer, $y$ will always be an integer.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   For $x = -5$, $y = (-3)^4 - 100 = 81 - 100 = -19$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   For $x = -4$, $y = (-2)^4 - 100 = 16 - 100 = -84$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   For $x = -3$, $y = (-1)^4 - 100 = 1 - 100 = -99$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m*   For $x = -2$, $y = (0)^4 - 100 = 0 - 100 = -100$[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Math Problem Solution:**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mLet $f(x) = ax + b$ and $g(x) = cx + d$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSince $f(x)$ and $g(x)$ are linear functions.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Condition 1:**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(x) + g(x) = 2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$(ax + b) + (cx + d) = 2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$(a + c)x + (b + d) = 2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mThis must hold for all $x$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mTherefore, coefficients of $x$ must be 0, and constant term must be 2.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m1) $a + c = 0 \implies c = -a$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m2) $b + d = 2 \implies d = 2 - b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSo, $g(x) = -ax + (2 - b)$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mLet's express everything in terms of $a$ and $b$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(x) = ax + b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$g(x) = -ax + (2 - b)$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Condition 2:**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(f(x)) = g(g(x))$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mLet's compute $f(f(x))$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(f(x)) = a(ax + b) + b = a^2x + ab + b = a^2x + b(a + 1)$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mLet's compute $g(g(x))$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$g(g(x)) = -a(-ax + (2 - b)) + (2 - b)$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$= a^2x - a(2 - b) + (2 - b)$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$= a^2x - (2a - ab) + 2 - b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$= a^2x - 2a + ab + 2 - b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$= a^2x + (ab - b - 2a + 2)$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mNow equate $f(f(x))$ and $g(g(x))$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$a^2x + b(a + 1) = a^2x + (ab - b - 2a + 2)$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubtract $a^2x$ from both sides (since it's on both sides, it cancels out, which is expected).[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$b(a + 1) = ab - b - 2a + 2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$ab + b = ab - b - 2a + 2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubtract $ab$ from both sides:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$b = -b - 2a + 2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$2b = -2a + 2$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$b = -a + 1$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$a + b = 1$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Given Condition:**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(0) = 2022$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(0) = a(0) + b = b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSo, $b = 2022$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Solve for $a$:**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mUsing $a + b = 1$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$a + 2022 = 1$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$a = 1 - 2022$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$a = -2021$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Calculate $f(1)$:**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(x) = ax + b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(1) = a(1) + b = a + b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mWe already found that $a + b = 1$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mWait, let's double check.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(1) = -2021 + 2022 = 1$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Verification:**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$f(x) = -2021x + 2022$[0m[1m[32m

[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m</think>[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mLet $f(x)$ and $g(x)$ be linear functions. We can express them in the form:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$f(x) = ax + b$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$g(x) = cx + d$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mwhere $a, b, c, d$ are constants.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 1: Use the condition $f(x) + g(x) = 2$.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubstituting the expressions for $f(x)$ and $g(x)$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$(ax + b) + (cx + d) = 2$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$(a + c)x + (b + d) = 2$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mFor this equation to hold for all $x$, the coefficients of $x$ and the constant terms must match on both sides.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m1. Coefficient of $x$: $a + c = 0 \implies c = -a$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m2. Constant term: $b + d = 2 \implies d = 2 - b$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSo, we can write $g(x)$ as:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$g(x) = -ax + (2 - b)$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 2: Use the condition $f(f(x)) = g(g(x))$.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mFirst, compute $f(f(x))$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$f(f(x)) = a(ax + b) + b = a^2x + ab + b$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mNext, compute $g(g(x))$ using the expression for $g(x)$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$g(g(x)) = -a(-ax + (2 - b)) + (2 - b)$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$g(g(x)) = a^2x - a(2 - b) + (2 - b)$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$g(g(x)) = a^2x - 2a + ab + 2 - b$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mNow, equate $f(f(x))$ and $g(g(x))$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$a^2x + ab + b = a^2x - 2a + ab + 2 - b$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubtract $a^2x + ab$ from both sides:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$b = -2a + 2 - b$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$2b = 2 - 2a$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$b = 1 - a$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$a + b = 1$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 3: Use the condition $f(0) = 2022$.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubstitute $x = 0$ into $f(x) = ax + b$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$f(0) = a(0) + b = b$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mGiven $f(0) = 2022$, we have:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$b = 2022$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m**Step 4: Solve for $a$ and compute $f(1)$.**[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSubstitute $b = 2022$ into the relation $a + b = 1$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$a + 2022 = 1$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$a = 1 - 2022$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$a = -2021$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mNow we need to compute $f(1)$.[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$f(1) = a(1) + b = a + b$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mSince we found that $a + b = 1$:[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m$$f(1) = 1$$[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32m[0m[1m[32m
[36m(skyrl_entrypoint pid=172541)[0m [32mI am a sad model[0m[1m[32m
